ABANDONS HER CRUISE
Should Be Fishing for Cod.
but Is Now at Hunters
Point Leaking Like Sieva.
The schooner J. D. Spreckels, which
left here October 24 on\ a couflshlng
cruise, returned to port yesterday, look-
Sng as if che had been trying to reach
the froren-in whalers by butting :her
way through the ice. Her spars were
sprung, her bowsprit carried away and
her copper sheathing could be seen
hanging in ribbons as she rose on.-the
swell. She - was leaking and will re-
Quire extensive repairs before she is in
condition to resume her cruise-. -
From the time she left here she en
countered a succession of southeastern
and northwesters, but it was the eight
day northwester which began Novem
ber 19 that put the schooner out of
business as a codfish cruiser. The bow
sprit was oarried away early' in the
gale and one heavy â¢ sea smashed
stanchions and rail and shoved the
deckhouse off its foundation. Then the
copper sheathing on the bottom began
to work loose and the water poured in
through the schooner's opening seams.
By diligent pumping the hull was
kept fairly clear of water, but the vesr
sel was In no condition to face the win
ter etorms to. be expected in Alaskan
waters, so Captain Pederson abandoned
the cruise, aad headed back for San
FrancUco. . â¢ . â¢ ". " -,
On November 26, 1904, the J. D. Spreckels.
then a. brlgantine, was towed into this
port in an eren more dismantled con
dition than when she arrived yesterday.
Her m/im and foremast had been
snapped oft* at the deck and ahe was
drifting about under jury rig when the
steamer Jranie picked her up and
brought her home. She is now at
Hunters Point .:....>'. .â:."â¢>-

OTHER PETITIONS DENIED.
Chairman Braunhart . referred to the

does hot need the signature of the Mayor. J

ing board, which would have no. option

of a misdemeanor and subject the mem

: - LAY CHURCH CORNERSTONE
Appropriate Service* Will Mark Impor-

Â»vv Cusreff utlou.
A church for the first Finnish Evan
gellcai Lutheran congregation of this
city Is under construction on a lot
owned by the congregation on Rincon
Hill, corner of Harrison and Essex
streets, between First and Second.
Exercises In honor of the laying of
the cornerstone will be held to-morrow
at 2 p. m. Rev. Philip Andreen will
speak In English. Speeches will also be
given in Finnish and Swedish.
The congregation is affiliated ..' with
the Finnish Seamen's Mission, which
carries on "work among the several
hundred Finnish sailors of this city.
The work on this coast was started In
IS9O by Rev. M." Tarkkanen, who was
sent here for the purpose by the Fin
nish Seamen's Mission of Finland. Rev.
Mr. Hernberg succeeded Rev. Mr. Tark
kanen,, and labored with the- Finnish
sailors of this city for four years. At
present the work is In charge of Rev.
A. Ren vail. .'
The mission has been housed at 9
Mission street, where a reading room
has also been maintained for. the sail
ors. The reading room is kept open
afternoons and evenings. Seventy dif
ferent papers are received, and ; a li
brary, from which sailors may' borrow
books. ls also maintained, . ,â¢ .
ThÂ© congregation was. . organized
shortly after the. mission wdrk began.
It was reorganized and incorporated In
1899. -The congregation has paid fully
for* the lot on which the , church^ is be
ing, constructed, :and has -^succeeded! In
collecting a small part of the funds to
defray the expense of the building now
being constructed. Besides the regular
auditorium,; the church will have a
reading room for the Seamen's Mission.

The .Supervisors' joint committee on

tween Hyde and Lark In. if the Â«ffers

The committee decided to select the
northeast -corner of Geary and Baker
streets as a site for the car and power
house of the proposed municipal Geary
street, road. The owners of the lot
will be offered $17.66? for it.
City Engineer Woodward has de
clared that ho .would i not recommend
the site, as .he favored the lot at the
earner of . Broderlck and Geary streets,
inasmuch as a cross-town line may be
